I used to come here as a kid, and I have fond memories of all the cool treasures of the marketplace. It shifted from a true flea market where people sell their home items, to a primarily Hispanic store where reoccurring vendors sell the same junk every week. There is nothing wrong with that if you are looking for good fruit, candy, veggies and some clothing. - They will keep your deposit no matter what and charge you even more when you move out.
- They charge you for everything, water, hot water, gas, trash, parking, and a lot of other fees so you should add at least $250 + rent.
- Good look trying to find another parking if you have 2 cars.
- Cars getting broken into all the time, and security is just a joke here.
- Getting packages is almost impossible. You will have to go and get them yourself from the local postal office. My packages are getting lost all the time.
- Everything is about money here and I truly mean it.

Pros,
- Clean apartments.
-  Washer and dryer in unit.< /Review>

<resp>None<//resp>< review>
First thing first: All the 5 and 4 star ratings that you see here, were sponsored by the property manager! The property incentivize residents in return for high ratings on yelp.

Pros: Close to Downtown San Jose.

Cons:
1. Majority of the tenants in this complex are students from San Jose State University. 7-8 individuals living in a single apartment.
Irrespective of time of day/night, there is always somebody on the phone in the patio or the corridor/hallways/Balconies or on the street below your apartment. Every night there is a frat party. There are Loud and obnoxious neighbor.

2. The property manager(E) and her assistant(G) are racist AF. Anytime you go to them with a complaint, they argue with you and it always end up in a verbal argument. They always retaliate with an eviction notice for minor little thing. Sooner or later you start complaining  in the fear of retaliation.

3. Poor Security: There has always been security issues at Villa Torino. The Management has failed to address these issues over the past years. Instead of improving security, the spent money on the look and feel of the community and even renovating the leasing office. The cost of adding security cameras and a DVR is much less compared to the amount they have spent on the effing planters. Every year, during the tax season the mailboxes get broken into. Apartments have been broken into in broad daylight. Residents have been attacked by homeless. Homeless have been seen wandering around in the community on several occasion. Bike and other items have been stolen from the patio/balconies of the apartments(even 3rd floor apartments!). Cars are broken into in the parking garage almost every month. The main entrances of the building are always broken and the locks don't work. There is an "off campus" security company, every time you call them, they show up more than an hour later. The tenants security is the lowest priority for EL and Gr.

4. AirBnb: At one point of time, the community had at least 3 apartments available on AirBnb. The management (Eli and Gre) were fully aware of these units, but they chose not to take any action(who knows what they got in return). There were random guests(of all kind) staying in those BnBs. The management had to shut it down after some backlash. They might have moved to VRBO or some thing else.

5. Appliances: Old and barely works. The dryers in the apartments are so old, it takes 2-3 cycles to dry your clothes. The Dish washer is a totally different beast(in a negative sense).

6. Elevators: Majority of the time the elevators in the community are broken and under repair. (Imagine carrying your Costco groceries up the stairs.)

7. Gym: Small overcrowded gym full of residents who lack basic gym etiquette.

8. Rules : The rules which are laid out by the management, change very frequently. The same set of rules don't apply to all the apartments. The management is lenient towards some apartments while the others get eviction notice.

9. Security Deposit: Needless to say, when moving out, don't have any expectation of getting any of security deposit back. They keep the security deposit in the name of "cleaning", even if they renovate the whole apartment after you move out.

Overall, these days there are a lot more options in Downtown San Jose. Pay $50-100 more, but stay away from Villa Torino and their rude Property Managers (Elis** and Greg).<//review>

<review>1st finally trying this location here and its during covid-19.
Set up was clean and distance was easy.
Used the self kiosk to place the order and pay.

Food came out pretty good, and we had it togo.

Kamikaze fries were great. Love the waffle fries and the sweet bulgolgi beef then mixed with the SRIRACHA sauce.  Love the sweet heat factor.

Chicken tacos are a must each time we come to a koja kitchen. Something about the wasabi flavor on it makes me want one everytime I visit.

Bulgolgi beef bun burger with added egg was good. Love their rice buns but having it in a bun held up better, but still good either way you try it.

The pulled pork bowl was ok, the coconut on the pork gives it such a great taste,and the salad was mostly dry cause the dressing ended up in the rice, that was not to good.

Not sure but the masago was missing on 3 items. Not sure what happened, wasn't told it was out.

Cool spot, good food like other kojas.

They do sell masks here, from re-usable to one time uses. And a few colors too. During covid-19.</review>< pics>

< Text>
I came here as a yelp Elite invited guest.   The restaurant is right at the k Street light rail...so you will need to park a block away...which is not too far.

The entrance to the restaurant is through the black iron fence...there is no side entrance.

The staff is friendly and greeted me upon arrival. They were very busy...yeah for them.

There is inside and outdoor seating whichever you prefer.

I was able to try the Korean Buffalo wing...soy garlic wing...kamikaze fries...crispy chicken nuggets...and braised pork bowl.

The wings had great flavor...not as crispy as I like.  The Korean Buffalo sauce definitely had heat with a little sweet...it was so good...I just wished they were more crispy...

The kamikaze fries...mmm. they start with a bed of crispy criss cross fries...then they are topped with minced Korean BBQ beef...oh my goodness the flavor was so good...COUPLED with kitchen red sauce..if you don't like spicy...ask them to hold the spice...Japanese mayo and green onions...these are very filling and delicious.

Crispy chicken nuggets...these are so good. I really liked the batter on them they were crispy and tender.  These are brined in sake...and they put a drizzle of honey Sriracha sauce on them...I wished there was more sauce...it was that good...

The braised pork bowl...now this was my favorite...oh my goodness...the pork is braised in a miso coconut broth...then it's coupled with a garlic aioli...and other things...

The meat is kind of like a shredded meat with everything mixed in and served with white rice.

The food here is so delicious...

The also sell boba teas..lemonade and soda...beer ect.

If your downtown around 9th and k street...you should try this place...</Text>

< Review>
Confusing online menu, it's in English but badly-translated and neither I nor my wife (a native Chinese speaker) can figure out what the dishes are; it would be better to put the Chinese name beside each one so we can read it ourselves.

Phone ordering is confusing: the staff often don't know what dishes are available even if it's something we've gotten here before (happens even if we order in Chinese).

Frequent issues with the credit card machine, sometimes this causes you to have to wait a while and your food gets cold.

The food is good but we might not order again because it's just too hard to order and pick up.</Review>

The drink machine is serve yourself with a lot of choices, so that's good for soda drinkers. There is also tea and less sugary drinks.
There are several types of salsa to try as well. The green is very flavorful and the medium red is a good choice.
Get the app to enjoy deals and on line discounts. The Jimmy John's loyalty program is worth signing up for. Hopefully there is one within driving range of your home or work.

NON-MEMBERS: BE ADVISED. LONG LINE WAITS. Not to be dramatic, but at one point while we were waiting in line it was so bad my 4.5 year old started crying and said, "Dad, can we please just leave and go to the water front park?" (And it wasn't a typical 4-year-old bratty/whining cry. It was a genuine sad/disappointed cry.) Basically what happened was, we got there at Noon and were close to the front of the "Non-member" line, but we didn't get in to the actual pool area until 1pm, and that was only because at 12:50 (20 minutes after the the session opened) I went up to the lifeguard who was processing everyone (members) in and asked her when they were going to start to also process the non-members. She said that she was going to process all of the members first before she started the non-members (which at the rate things were going and how many members there still were in line we MAYBE would have gotten into the pool at 1:30.) So I asked her to double check with a supervisor on their policy (because if that were the case we would've left.) Thankfully she checked because when she came back they started processing the non-members as well. All that to say, it was a very stressful and very disappointing way to start off what (thankfully) ended up being a fun afternoon at the pool. And although it ended up being fun, unless they change their process or non-member/resident price, I don't plan on going back. It's just not worth it for price, wait in line, and limited time alowed inside. I get that members/residents have priority, but still..it doesn't need to be this bad. (Maybe process people who are in line early and have a separate staging area where people who are already processed can wait and then go right in when the session starts?)
